MANUAL OF VICTUALLING.—APPENDICES,
Nothing contained in these Appendices is to be understood to supersede
the King’s Regulations and Admiralty Instructions, but the regulations
and instructions given in the former are to be regarded as supplementing
those contained in the latter.
All directions issued from time to time which add to or modify these
Appendices are to be carefully noted in all copies in use in ELM. Ships
and Naval Shore Establishments.
By Command of Their Lordships,
To all Commander s-in-CMef, Flag Officers,
Captains, Commanders and Commanding
Officers of IJ.M. Ships and Vessels, and
all others concerned.

APPENDIX A.
ISSUING STRENGTH OF SPIRIT.
Whenever spirit has become reduced 10 per cent, or more below proof, the
following additional quantities for every gallon of such spirit may be (a) substituted
for water, or (6) added to the neat spirit issued to Chief Petty Officers and Petty
Officers, in order that the spirit ration may be issued at its ordinary strength :
GUIs.
10 per cent, under proof ... ... ... ... ... 1£

2. To ascertain the quantity of water which should be added to strong rum to
reduce it to the issuing strength of 5 per cent, under proof (Art. 1904, King’s
Regulations and Admiralty Instructions), multiply the quantity to be reduced by
the actual strength and divide the result by the issuing strength. The difference l
between this result and the quantity to be reduced gives the number of gallons
of water to be added.
3. Hydrometers for testing spirit are supplied to all ships commissioning for
foreign service, and to flag ships and depot ships (only) at Home.

APPENDIX C.
INSTRUCTIONS FOR THE SELECTION AND DESPATCH OF SAMPLES.
Whenever it is necessary for samples of any description to be forwarded for
examination or analysis, care should be exercised that they fairly represent the
bulk from which they were drawn.
The receptacles in which the samples are placed should be quite clean, and new
corks only should be used in closing all bottles.
Such articles as butter or lard should be forwarded in wide-mouthed bottles or
earthenware jars, securely corked so as to exclude the air.
The importance of securing the utmost promptitude in the transmission of
samples, more particularly fresh milk, cannot be too strongly impressed upon the
responsible Officers. Notice of the despatch of the samples, giving all necessary
particulars, should be forwarded in a separate cover at the same time as the samples.
A label should also be attached to the sample, giving the date of communication,
description of article, and all particulars that it is considered would be of assistance
in the proper examination.
When several samples are forwarded at the same time and in the same package,
the outside of the package should be clearly marked with the name of the sending
establishment, &c., so that it can be easily identified on receipt.
{See also Chapter IX, Section 18.)

APPENDIX E.
RULES FOR BREADMAKING COMPETITION.
With a view to standardising as far as possible the conditions under which Fleet
Breadmaking Competitions are conducted, the following general arrangements for
such competitions have been approved :
(1) The competition to be divided into two sections, viz. :
(A) Ships with bakeries.
(B) Ships without bakeries, but galley-baked bread from ships with bakeries
may be entered in this section.
(2) Section (B) is included to encourage Cook ratings to maintain a high standard
in breadmaking, and to produce satisfactory bread when circumstances require
breadmaking in ships without the proper appliances,
(3) Only ships’ Cook ratings to be eligible to compete. All ships present,
in which ships’ Cook ratings are borne, to compete in their appropriate section :
galley-baked bread from ships with bakeries to be optional.
(4) Only one entry to be made by ships competing, except that ships with
bakeries may enter galley-baked bread in Section (B) in addition to bakery bread in
Section (A).
(5) Galleys provided solely for officers’ messes not to be used for making bread
for the competition.
(6) Bread for the competition to be made only from Service ingredients used
in making bread issued on board. The bread entered for the competition to be
taken from that baked on the preceding day.
In the case of Section (B), loaves to be selected from a special batch of 20 lbs.
baked on the day prior to the competition.
(7) Loaves entered for the competition to be :
Section (A).
One outside loaf broken from a bar of two or more tin loaves ; one cobourg
loaf not baked in a tin.
Section ( B).
Two loaves as may be directed by the authority arranging the competition.
Each loaf entered to be of nominal 2 lbs. weight.
(8) Scale for the award of marks to be as follows ;
External appearance ... ... ... ... 25
Colour and texture of crumb ... ... ... 25
Flavour ... ... ... ... ... ... 25
Volume and weight ... ... ... ... 25
Total 100
(9) Loaves to be sent to the place of competition accompanied by a certificate
giving the following particulars : —-
(a) Name of ship.
(b) Section (A or B) of competition.
(c) Name, rating, official number and port division of the Cook rating who
made the bread.
(d) Date and time the bread was taken out of the oven.


(10) Aa many Cook ratings as can be spared to be assembled at the place of
competition to hear the results announced, to witness the presentation of any
trophies there may be, and to view the exhibits.
(11) Bread sent for competition to be expended “Used for breadmaking
competition,” and given to a local charity if desired.
(12) A report of the competition, giving particulars of the general standard of
exhibits, marks obtained by each ship, and the names, etc., of the Cook ratings who
made the winning loaves, to be forwarded to the Admiralty.
(13) Administrative authorities to issue such detailed instructions as may be
necessary for the conduct of the competition : a copy of these Orders to be forwarded
with the report referred to in paragraph 12.
Appendix E — continued.


APPENDIX P.
POWERS OF PUBLIC HEALTH OFFICERS—UNSOUND FOOD.
In case it may at any time be necessary to call in the assistance of the Local
Authority, the following extracts from the Food and Drugs Act, 1938, giving
particulars as to their powers, may be useful:—
Unsound Food.
9. —(1) A person who— Penalty for
(а) sells, or offers or exposes for sale, or has in his possession for the purpose of ungf ’ unc f
sale or of preparation for sale ; or . food.
(б) deposits with, or consigns to, any person for the purpose of sale or of
preparation for sale,
any food intended for, but unfit for, human consumption shall, subject to the
provisions of this section, be guilty of an offence.
(2) Where food in respect of which an offence under paragraph (a) of the
preceding subsection has been committed was sold to the offender by some other
person, that person also shall, subject to the provisions of this section, be guilty
of an offence.
(3) Where a person is charged with an offence under paragraph (ft) of subsection
(1) of this section or under the last preceding subsection, it shall be a defence for him
to prove either that he gave notice to the person with whom he deposited, or to whom
he consigned or sold, the food in question that it was not intended for human
consumption, or that, at the time when he delivered or dispatched it to that person,
either it was fit for human consumption or he did not know, and could not with
reasonable diligence have ascertained, that it was unfit for human consumption.
(4) A person guilty of an offence under this section shall be liable to a fine not
exceeding fifty pounds, or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months,
or to both such a fine and such imprisonment.
(5) If a person licensed under this Act, or the Public Health (London) Act, 1936,
to keep a slaughter-house is convicted of an offence under this section, the court may,
in addition to any other penalty, cancel his licence.
(6) The justice of the peace before whom any food is brought under the next
succeeding section may, but need not, be a member of the court before which a
person is charged with an offence under this section in relation to that food.
10. —(1) An authorised officer of a local authority may at all reasonable times Examina-
examine any food intended for human consumption which has been sold, or is offered Lon of food
or exposed for sale, or is in the possession of, or has been deposited with or consigned anc * ae^zure
to, any person for the purpose of sale or of preparation for sale, and, if it appears to f J 0^ n8 ° Und
him to be unfit for human consumption, may seize it and remove it in order to have 1
it dealt with by a justice of the peace.
(2) An officer who seizes any food under the preceding subsection shall inform
the person in whose possession it was found of his intention to have it dealt with by a
justice of the peace, and any person who under the last preceding section might be
liable to a prosecution in respect of the food shall, if he attends before the justice
upon the application for its condemnation, be entitled to be heard and to call
witnesses.
(3) If it appears to a justice of the peace that any food brought before him,
whether seized under the provisions of this section or not, is unfit for human consump-
tion, he shall condemn it and order it to be destroyed, or to be so disposed of as
to prevent it from being used for human consumption.
(4) If a justice of the peace refuses to condemn any food seized under this Part
of this Act by an authorised officer of a local authority, the authority shall
compensate the owner of the food for any depreciation in its value resulting from
its seizure and removal.


Power to 12. If an authorised officer of a local authority has reason to suspect that any
cart, barrow or other vehicle, or any container contains any food intended for sale for
course of human consumption, or in the course of delivery after sale for human consumption,
transit he may examine the contents of the vehicle, or, as the case may be, of the container,
and for that purpose may, if necessary, detain the vehicle or the container, and, if
he finds any food which appears to him to be intended for, but unfit for, human
consumption, he may deal with it as food falling within subsection (1) of section
ten of this Act and subsections (2) to (4) of that section shall apply accordingly :
Provided that—
(а) nothing in this section shall authorise the examination of the contents of—
(i) any vehicle belonging to a railway company and used by them for the
purposes of their undertaking ; or
(ii) any authorised vehicle used for the purpose of his business as a carrier
of goods by a person holding an A licence or a B licence under
Part I of the Road and Rail Traffic Act, 1933 ; or
(iii) any container in the possession of a railway company or of any such
person as aforesaid as carriers or carrier thereof; and
(б) where the duties of an officer of customs and excise with respect to any
goods have not been wholly discharged, nothing in this section shall
authorise the examination of those goods without his consent.
Interpretation, &c.
Definitions. 100.- —(1) In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires—
“ authorised officer ” means, as respects any council, an officer of the counci
authorised by them in writing, either generally or specially, to act in
matters of any specified kind or in any specified matter and, for the
purposes of the provisions of this Act relating to the taking of samples,
includes a police constable so authorised with the approval of the police
authority concerned :
Provided that—
(a) the medical officer of health and sanitary inspector of a council
shall by virtue of their appointments be deemed to be
authorised officers for all the purposes of this Act ;
( b ) any member of the Royal College of Veterinary Surgeons
employed by the council for the purpose of the inspection
of food shall be deemed to be an authorised officer for the
purpose of the examination and seizure of meat under the
provisions of this Act relating to unsound food ;
(c) no officer of a council other than the medical officer of health,
a sanitary inspector or a member of the Royal College of
Veterinary Surgeons employed as aforesaid shall be authorised
to act in relation to the examination and seizure of meat.

Fearnought gauntlets ... ... Prs. 15.
2. The allowances calculated on the above are maxima, and the quantities of
sea boots and oilskin clothing cover the full war requirements both for weather
protection and for decontamination parties.
3. Oilskin coats and leggings may be drawn in lieu of oilskin jackets and trousers
up to 25 per cent, of allowance.
4. Senior officers may authorise less than the full allowances to be carried when
conditions render this necessary or desirable ; but the full allowances of anti-flash
clothing, of protective clothing for fire and repair parties, and of oilskin hoods and
gloves, and sufficient oilskin suits and rubber boots to ensure that the full quantities
required for the equipment of decontamination parties, on the basis of 2 suits for
each man in the party, are always available should be carried whenever
practicable.

Note 3.—If going to a Foreign Station, 10 per cent, of the total quantities in addition
to be in the Accountant Officers’ charge, with the exception of kettles.
Note 4. —Harbour tenders employed conveying supernumeraries are to be furnished
according to the scale in Col. 2, and with an additional quantity for a number of persons
not exceeding 100.

Note.—Leaders, Destroyers, &c., with complements over 150
should demand
additional articles in proportion, as required.
Note. —Supplied only to ships with patt. 7a galley ranges. The tins should be
stowed in the ovens as follows :—
Large Oven.
Upper Compartment. —Four 8-lb. tins side by side, each with one end to the side
of the oven ; seven 2-lb. tins end to end along the other side and across the front.
Lower Compartment. —Six 8-lb. tins in pairs, end to end, along the depth of the
oven.
Small Oven.
Three 8-lb. tins, end to end, along the depth of the oven in both upper and lower
compartments.

Appendix J —Part lll — continued.


GENERAL NOTES ON SCALES Nos. 1-50.
General Note 1. —Where an item appears in a scale and no quantities are shown
(this occurs principally in Optional sections), a mess may demand the article
for
supply against the monetary allowance for that section.
The option is limited to the articles shown in each scale.
General Note 2. —The sign * indicates the Permanent stores which may
be
condemned on board and written off charge by certificate.
Special Notes.
Note 3. Captains ( D) in Flotilla Leaders. —Captains (D) in
flotilla leaders
are
allowed mess traps as follows ; —
Table Ware. —As for a Flag Captain (Seale 3) with the
option of drawing
necessary additional gear within the scale for a Captain
(Scale 2).
Pantry and Galley Hardware. —To Scale 4.
Note 4. Commanding Officers of Destroyers, Minesweepers
, <&c. —Officers
of
Ward Room rank in command of destroyers, minesweepers, &c. (i.e., ships which
are not entitled to separate sets of Commanding Officers’ mess
china and earthenware of Commanding Officers’ pattern as follow
traps) may draw
s :— ■
In addition to the articles supplied for the Ward Room mess.

1937 SCALES OF MESS GEAR.


1937 SCALES FOE, FLAG AND COMMANDING OFFICERS’ MESSES.
Flag and Commanding Officers may vary the descriptions and quantities of
any of the stores shown in Scales Nos. 1-4, provided that the value
of the stores demanded (calculated at the rates shown in
the scales) does not exceed the respective monetary allowances for Permanent and Consumable
Stores allowed
for the mess.

1937 SCALES FOR WARD ROOM MESSES OF I TO 12 OFFICERS.
These scales (Nos. 5-11) do NOT apply to Submarines, Trawlers or small craft for which special scales are provided.
See General Notes 1 and 2 and Special Note 4 on Scales Nos. 1-50.
Ward Room Messes may vary the description and quantities of any of the stores shown in scales Nos. 5-1 1, provided that the value of the stores
demanded (calculated at the rates shown in the scales) does not exceed the respective monetary allowances for Permanent and Consumable stores
allowed for the Mess.

Scales Nos. 5-11


1937 SCALES FOR WARD ROOM MESSES OF 13 TO 100 OFFICERS.
(Scales Nos. 12-24.)
See General Notes 1 and 2 on Scales Nos. 1 — 50.
Ward Room Messes may vary the descriptions and quantities of any of the stores shown in Scales Nos. 12 to 24 provided that the value of
the stores demanded (calculated at the rates shown in the scales) does not exceed the respective monetary allowances for Permanent and
Consumable stores allowed for the Mess. The monetary allowance for those messes above 40 for which no scale is provided is to be calculated
as a proportion of the nearest valued scale {e.g., for a mess of 43 officers the value will be 43/40ths of the value of Scale 19, and for a mess of 47
it will be 47/50ths of the value of Scale 20).

(Scales Nos. 56-60.)
GENERAL NOTES ON SCALES Nos. 56-63.
Paymasters’ Implements and Galley Gear.
-Paymasters’ Implements ~~{a) First supplies on commissioning.-- Detailed demands are to bo furnished for the articles and quantities required.
npracticable for detailed demands to be furnished and the demand simply states “A set to Scale No the articles and quantities
appropriate typical scale, excluding all Optional items, will be supplied,
and descriptions of bread tins required must, however, invariably be stated.
Permanent stores which may be condemned on board and written-olf by certificate are indicated by an asterisk.
-Galley Gear. —The provisions of Note 1 {a) above apply to galley gear.
ve the option of varying the quantities of any of the items shown in the scales of galley gear Nos. 56-60 and of drawing supplies of the items
shese scales for which no quantities are given, provided that the value {calculated at the rate shown in the scales) of the total quantities of
ms of galley gear drawn for use in the galley and bakery does not exceed the “ monetary allowance ” for the authorised complement of ratings calculated,
er 25 men shown at the head of the scales. The number of men in the complement is to be taken to the nearest 25 men downwards in
e allowance {e.g., 824 men = 800 ; 830 men = 825 ; 860 men = 850).
